--></div><div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n<div id="mw-indicator-pp-default" class="mw-indicator"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Protection_policy#semi" title="This article is semi-protected."><img alt="Page semi-protected" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Padlock-silver.svg/20px-Padlock-silver.svg.png" width="20" height="20" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Padlock-silver.svg/40px-Padlock-silver.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="128" data-file-height="128" /></a></div>\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of countries by GDP (nominal)</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For countries by GDP based on purchasing power parity, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">List of countries by GDP (PPP)</a>.</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n\n</p>\n<table border="0" cellpadding="2" cellspacing="0" style="float:right;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td><div class="timeline-wrapper"><map name="timeline_45cabf722ffec5de02631bda1f6ccce0"></map><img usemap="#timeline_45cabf722ffec5de02631bda1f6ccce0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/45cabf722ffec5de02631bda1f6ccce0.png" /></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center; font-size:100%;">Largest economies by nominal GDP in 2017<sup id="cite_ref-GDP_IMF_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GDP_IMF-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">Gross domestic product</a> (GDP) is the <a href="/wiki/Market_value" title="Market value">market value</a> of all final goods and services from a nation in a given year.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Countries are sorted by nominal <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> estimates from financial and statistical institutions, which are calculated at market or government official <a href="/wiki/Exchange_rate" title="Exchange rate">exchange rates</a>. Nominal GDP does not take into account differences in the <a href="/wiki/Cost_of_living" title="Cost of living">cost of living</a> in different countries, and the results can vary greatly from one year to another based on fluctuations in the <a href="/wiki/Exchange_rate" title="Exchange rate">exchange rates</a> of the country\'s <a href="/wiki/Currency" title="Currency">currency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Such fluctuations may change a country\'s ranking from one year to the next, even though they often make little or no difference in the standard of living of its population.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Comparisons of national wealth are also frequently made on the basis of <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> (PPP), to adjust for differences in the cost of living in different countries. PPP largely removes the exchange rate problem, but has its own drawbacks; it does not reflect the value of economic output in <a href="/wiki/International_trade" title="International trade">international trade</a>, and it also requires more estimation than nominal GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> On the whole, PPP per capita figures are less spread than nominal GDP per capita figures.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_United_States" title="Economy of the United States">United States</a> is the world\'s largest economy with a GDP of approximately $19.39 trillion, notably due to <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">high average incomes</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by population">a large population</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> capital investment, moderate <a href="/wiki/Unemployment_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Unemployment rate">unemployment</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> high consumer spending,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> a relatively young population,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> and technological innovation.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Tuvalu" title="Economy of Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a> is the world\'s smallest national economy, with a GDP of about $32 million, because of its very small population, a lack of natural resources, reliance on foreign aid, negligible <a href="/wiki/Capital_investment" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital investment">capital investment</a>, demographic problems, and low average incomes.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although the <a href="/wiki/List_of_IMF_ranked_countries_by_past_and_projected_GDP_(nominal)" class="mw-redirect" title="List of IMF ranked countries by past and projected GDP (nominal)">rankings of national economies</a> have changed considerably over time, the United States has maintained its top position since the <a href="/wiki/Gilded_Age" title="Gilded Age">Gilded Age</a>, a time period in which its economy saw rapid expansion, surpassing the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing dynasty</a> in aggregate output.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ChinaKnow_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChinaKnow-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Since China\'s <a href="/wiki/Chinese_economic_reform" title="Chinese economic reform">transition to a market-based economy</a> through privatisation and deregulation,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> the country has seen its ranking increase from ninth in 1978 to second to only the United States in 2016 as economic growth accelerated and its share of global nominal GDP surged from 2% in 1980 to 15% in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-ChinaKnow_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChinaKnow-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GDP_IMF_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GDP_IMF-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> India has also experienced a similar economic boom since the implementation of <a href="/wiki/Economic_liberalisation_in_India" title="Economic liberalisation in India">economic liberalisation</a> in the early 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/Supranational_union" title="Supranational union">supranational entities</a> are included, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> is the second largest economy in the world. It was the largest from 2004, <a href="/wiki/2004_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2004 enlargement of the European Union">when ten countries joined the union</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> to 2014, after which it was surpassed by the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-IMF_Groups_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMF_Groups-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first list includes estimates compiled by the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Outlook" title="World Economic Outlook">World Economic Outlook</a>, the second list shows the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>\'s data, and the third list includes data compiled by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Statistics_Division" title="United Nations Statistics Division">United Nations Statistics Division</a>. The IMF  definitive data for the past year and estimates for the current year are published twice a year in April and October. Several economies which are not considered to be countries (the world, the European Union, and some <a href="/wiki/Dependent_territories" class="mw-redirect" title="Dependent territories">dependent territories</a>) are included in the lists because they appear in the sources as distinct economies. These economies are italicized and not ranked in the charts, but are listed where applicable.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox"
